- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms

- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Compliance Audit: Kafka Audit Logging and Authorization Events

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in `apache/kafka` that produce audit log entries for authorization decisions. Search `core/src/main/scala/` and `clients/src/main/java/` for files that log `ALLOWED` or `DENIED` authorization events, reference `AuditLogger`, or implement audit trail functionality for ACL decisions. Report the file path and the class name producing audit events.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the compliance domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've completed the task and created the answer file. 

## Summary

I found the audit logging implementation for Apache Kafka authorization decisions. The primary source is:

**`StandardAuthorizerData.java`** (metadata/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/metadata/authorizer/) - This class contains:

1. **`logAuditMessage()`** method - Logs authorization decisions at appropriate levels:
   - ALLOWED operations: logged at DEBUG level (when actual access granted) or TRACE level
   - DENIED operations: logged at INFO level (when access explicitly denied) or TRACE level

2. **`buildAuditMessage()`** method - Constructs detailed audit messages including:
   - Principal (user)
   - Authorization decision (Allowed/Denied)
   - Operation type
   - Client host
   - Resource details
   - Request type
   - ACL rule matched

The audit logging is integrated through:
- **`StandardAuthorizer.java`** - Delegates authorization to StandardAuthorizerData
- **`Action.java`** - Contains `logIfAllowed()` and `logIfDenied()` flags
- **`AuthorizationResult.java`** - Defines ALLOWED and DENIED enum values

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive details about all files, symbols, and the audit logging chain.

If any DENY ACLs match, the operation is denied, no matter how\n224:      * many ALLOW ACLs match. If neither ALLOW nor DENY ACLs match, we return the default\n225:      * result. In general it makes more sense to configure the default result to be\n226:      * DENY, but some people (and unit tests) configure it as ALLOW.\n227:      */\n228:     public AuthorizationResult authorize(\n229:         AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext,\n230:         Action action\n231:     ) {\n232:         if (action.resourcePattern().patternType() != LITERAL) {\n233:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Only literal resources are supported. Got: \" + action.resourcePattern().patternType());\n234:         }\n235:         KafkaPrincipal principal = baseKafkaPrincipal(requestContext);\n236:         final MatchingRule rule;\n237: \n238:         // Superusers are authorized to do anything.\n239:         if (superUsers.contains(principal.toString())) {\n240:             rule = SuperUserRule.INSTANCE;\n241:         } else if (!loadingComplete) {\n242:             throw new AuthorizerNotReadyException();\n243:         } else {\n244:             rule = findAclRule(\n245:                 matchingPrincipals(requestContext),\n246:                 requestContext.clientAddress().getHostAddress(),\n247:                 action\n248:             );\n249:         }\n250:         logAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule);\n251:         return rule.result();\n252:     }\n253: \n254:     private String buildAuditMessage(\n255:         KafkaPrincipal principal,\n256:         AuthorizableRequestContext context,\n257:         Action action,\n258:         MatchingRule rule\n259:     ) {\n260:         StringBuilder bldr = new StringBuilder();\n261:         bldr.append(\"Principal = \").append(principal);\n262:         bldr.append(\" is \").append(rule.result() == ALLOWED ? If false, no access is actually granted, the result is used\n291:                 // only to determine authorized operations. So log only at trace level.\n292:                 if (action.logIfAllowed() && auditLog.isDebugEnabled()) {\n293:                     auditLog.debug(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\n294:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\n295:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\n296:                 }\n297:                 return;\n298: \n299:             case DENIED:\n300:                 // logIfDenied is true if access to the resource was explicitly requested. Since this is an attempt\n301:                 // to access unauthorized resources, log at info level. If false, this is either a request to determine\n302:                 // authorized operations or a filter (e.g for regex subscriptions) to filter out authorized resources.\n303:                 // In this case, log only at trace level.\n304:                 if (action.logIfDenied()) {\n305:                     auditLog.info(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\n306:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\n307:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\n308:                 }\n309:         }\n310:     }\n311: \n312:     private MatchingRule findAclRule(\n313:         Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\n314:         String host,\n315:         Action action\n316:     ) {\n317:         // This code relies on the ordering of StandardAcl within the NavigableMap.\n318:         // Entries are sorted by resource type first, then REVERSE resource name.\n319:         // Therefore, we can find all the applicable ACLs by starting at\n320:         // (resource_type, resource_name) and stepping forwards until we reach\n321:         // an ACL with a resource name which is not a prefix of the current one.\n322:         // At that point, we need to search for if there are any more ACLs at\n323:         // the first divergence point.\n324:         //\n325:         // For example, when trying to authorize a TOPIC resource named foobar, we would\n326:         // start at element 2, and continue on to 3 and 4 following map:\n327:         //\n328:         // 1. rs=TOPIC rn=gar pt=PREFIX\n329:         // 2. rs=TOPIC rn=foobar pt=PREFIX\n330:         // 3. rs=TOPIC rn=foob pt=LITERAL\n331:         // 4. rs=TOPIC rn=foo pt=PREFIX\n332:         // 5. rs=TOPIC rn=fb pt=PREFIX\n333:         // 6. rs=TOPIC rn=fa pt=PREFIX\n334:         // 7. rs=TOPIC rn=f  pt=PREFIX\n335:         // 8. rs=TOPIC rn=eeee pt=LITERAL\n336:         //\n337:         // Once we reached element 5, we would jump to element 7.\n338:         MatchingRuleBuilder matchingRuleBuilder = new MatchingRuleBuilder(noAclRule);\n339:         StandardAcl exemplar = new StandardAcl(\n340:             action.resourcePattern().resourceType(),\n341:             action.resourcePattern().name(),\n342:             PatternType.UNKNOWN, // Note that the UNKNOWN value sorts before all others.\n343:             \"\",\n344:             \"\",\n345:             AclOperation.UNKNOWN,\n346:             AclPermissionType.UNKNOWN);\n347:         AclCache aclCacheSnapshot = aclCache;\n348:         checkSection(aclCacheSnapshot, action, exemplar, matchingPrincipals, host, matchingRuleBuilder);\n349:         if (matchingRuleBuilder.foundDeny()) {\n350:             return matchingRuleBuilder.build();\n351:         }\n352: \n353:         // In addition to ACLs for this specific resource name, there can also be wildcard\n354:         // ACLs that match any resource name. These are stored as type = LITERAL,\n355:         // name = \"*\". We search these next.\n356:         exemplar = new StandardAcl(\n357:             action.resourcePattern().resourceType(),\n358:             WILDCARD,\n359:             LITERAL,\n360:             \"\",\n361:             \"\",\n362:             AclOperation.UNKNOWN,\n363:             AclPermissionType.UNKNOWN);\n364:         checkSection(aclCacheSnapshot, action, exemplar, matchingPrincipals, host, matchingRuleBuilder);\n365:         return matchingRuleBuilder.build();\n366:     }\n367: \n368:     static int matchesUpTo(\n369:         String resource,\n370:         String pattern\n371:     ) {\n372:         int i = 0;\n373:         while (true) {\n374:             if (resource.length() == i) break;\n375:             if (pattern.length() == i) break;\n376:             if (resource.charAt(i) != pattern.charAt(i)) break;\n377:             i++;\n378:         }\n379:         return i;\n380:     }\n381: \n382:     private void checkSection(\n383:             AclCache aclCacheSnapshot, Action action,\n384:             StandardAcl exemplar,\n385:             Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\n386:             String host,\n387:             MatchingRuleBuilder matchingRuleBuilder\n388:     ) {\n389:         String resourceName = action.resourcePattern().name();\n390:         NavigableSet<StandardAcl> tailSet = aclCacheSnapshot.aclsByResource().tailSet(exemplar, true);\n391:         Iterator<StandardAcl> iterator = tailSet.iterator();\n392:         while (iterator.hasNext()) {\n393:             StandardAcl acl = iterator.next();\n394:             if (!acl.resourceType().equals(action.resourcePattern().resourceType())) {\n395:                 // We've stepped outside the section for the resource type we care about and\n396:                 // should stop scanning.\n397:                 break;\n398:             }\n399:             int matchesUpTo = matchesUpTo(resourceName, acl.resourceName());\n400:             if (matchesUpTo == acl.resourceName().length()) {\n401:                 if (acl.patternType() == LITERAL && matchesUpTo != resourceName.length()) {\n402:                     // This is a literal ACL whose name is a prefix of the resource name, but\n403:                     // which doesn't match it exactly. We should skip over this ACL, but keep\n404:                     // scanning in case there are any relevant PREFIX ACLs.\n405:                     continue;\n406:                 }\n407: \n408:             } else if (!(acl.resourceName().equals(WILDCARD) && acl.patternType() == LITERAL)) {\n409:                 // If the ACL resource name is NOT a prefix of the current resource name,\n410:                 // and we're not dealing with the special case of a wildcard ACL, we've\n411:                 // stepped outside of the section we care about. Scan for any other potential\n412:                 // prefix matches.\n413:                 exemplar = new StandardAcl(exemplar.resourceType(),\n414:                     exemplar.resourceName().substring(0, matchesUpTo),\n415:                     exemplar.patternType(),\n416:                     exemplar.principal(),\n417:                     exemplar.host(),\n418:                     exemplar.operation(),\n419:                     exemplar.permissionType());\n420:                 tailSet = aclCacheSnapshot.aclsByResource().tailSet(exemplar, true);\n421:                 iterator = tailSet.iterator();\n422:                 continue;\n423:             }\n424:             matchingRuleBuilder.hasResourceAcls = true;\n425:             AuthorizationResult result = findResult(action, matchingPrincipals, host, acl);\n426:             if (ALLOWED == result) {\n427:                 matchingRuleBuilder.allowAcl = acl;\n428:             } else if (DENIED == result) {\n429:                 matchingRuleBuilder.denyAcl = acl;\n430:                 return;\n431:             }\n432:         }\n433:     }\n434: \n435:     /**\n436:      * The set of operations which imply DESCRIBE permission, when used in an ALLOW acl.\n437:      */\n438:     private static final Set<AclOperation> IMPLIES_DESCRIBE =\n439:         Set.of(DESCRIBE, READ, WRITE, DELETE, ALTER);\n440: \n441:     /**\n442:      * The set of operations which imply DESCRIBE_CONFIGS permission, when used in an ALLOW acl.\n443:      */\n444:     private static final Set<AclOperation> baseKafkaPrincipal(AuthorizableRequestContext context) {\n459:         KafkaPrincipal sessionPrincipal = context.principal();\n460:         return sessionPrincipal.getClass().equals(KafkaPrincipal.class)\n461:             ? sessionPrincipal\n462:             : new KafkaPrincipal(sessionPrincipal.getPrincipalType(), sessionPrincipal.getName());\n463:     }\n464: \n465:     static Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals(AuthorizableRequestContext context) {\n466:         KafkaPrincipal sessionPrincipal = context.principal();\n467:         KafkaPrincipal basePrincipal = sessionPrincipal.getClass().equals(KafkaPrincipal.class)\n468:             ? sessionPrincipal\n469:             : new KafkaPrincipal(sessionPrincipal.getPrincipalType(), sessionPrincipal.getName());\n470:         return Set.of(basePrincipal, WILDCARD_KAFKA_PRINCIPAL);\n471:     }\n472: \n473:     /**\n474:      * Determine what the result of applying an ACL to the given action and request\n475:      * context should be. Note that this function assumes that the resource name matches;\n476:      * the resource name is not checked here.\n477:      *\n478:      * @param action             The input action.\n479:      * @param matchingPrincipals The set of input matching principals\n480:      * @param host               The input host.\n481:      * @param acl                The input ACL.\n482:      * @return                   null if the ACL does not match. The authorization result\n483:      *                           otherwise.\n484:      */\n485:     static AuthorizationResult findResult(Action action,\n486:                                           Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\n487:                                           String host,\n488:                                           StandardAcl acl) {\n489:         // Check if the principal matches. If it doesn't, return no result (null).\n490:         if (!matchingPrincipals.contains(acl.kafkaPrincipal())) {\n491:             return null;\n492:         }\n493:         // Check if the host matches. If it doesn't, return no result (null).\n494:         if (!acl.host().equals(WILDCARD) && !acl.host().equals(host)) {\n495:             return null;\n496:         }\n497:         // Check if the operation field matches. Here we hit a slight complication.\n498:         // ACLs for various operations (READ, WRITE, DELETE, ALTER), \"imply\" the presence\n499:         // of DESCRIBE, even if it isn't explicitly stated. A similar rule applies to\n500:         // DESCRIBE_CONFIGS.\n501:         //\n502:         // But this rule only applies to ALLOW ACLs.
